Heritage Park historically has been a great public park. Besides the basketball courts, skate park and children's playground. There is plenty of space for events, picnics, or even car shows. Whether it's sports or just plain exercise its a place for anyone to enjoy. There are several species of Trees and many different species of birds and i've even seen squirrels and a kit fox there once. I rate Heritage Park of East Bakersfield California five stars.< /Text>

<Text>VOLVO XC90 BRAKE DEFECTS: We purchased a 2017 Volvo XC90 from this dealership at the end of 2017. A few weeks before our first maintenance vist at roughly 12k miles we started noticing an intense shaking while driving on the freeway. So much so that we would pull over thinking something was broken on the vehicle. We live in Arizona so we took the vehicle to Scottsdale Volvo for maintenance. We we're told that they could find no issue in regards to the shaking but that our brakes we down to 20% life already. At 12k miles we had no brakes left. We asked them if that was normal to which they told us it depended on how we drove the vehicle. It has an "active" braking system they told us. Eventually we found out from one of the service techs that Volvo has a brake issue on the XC90. Basically if they do not use an organic (softer) pad, your brakes will sqeal like crazy. The problem is your brakes go out every year as a result of the organic pad, or twice a year if you drive alot. It's about $1100 for 4 new brake pads. We had our Volvo for a little over 2 years. About 40k miles in total on the vehicle. In that time we went through 9 rotors, and a few sets of brakes. And these we're not just worn rotors due to normal wear, they would end up being warped. One person we found online went through 2 sets of brake pads and rotors in 6 months. If you look hard enough you can find issues like this all over the internet for the XC90. Basically Volvo uses an organic brake pad to mask the real issue and then they tell you it's your braking habits and make you pay for it. But I've never heard of a vehicle that has brake pads that go out at 12k miles. And I would never consider that normal by any means. I've owned alot of vehicles but I've never had brakes go out sooner than 50k miles. It just seems bizarre that you would have to replace your brakes every year or "twice" if you drive alot. I have a truck that out weighs the XC90 by a long shot and I always get 80k miles out of those brake pads. Now, the brakes were just one issue we had. The intense shaking at high speeds was never resolved. And to my knowledge there's a few forums online for the same issue and no one has ever had any resolve. The problem was intermittent for us. You would be driving on the freeway and then all of the sudden you would feel this intense pounding like you had a cupped tire or something. We would pull over thinking something broke on the vehicle. We took it in to Scottsdale numerous times. They told us for them to fix anything we would have to duplicate the issue every time. And if we happened to duplicate the issue, they would try something and then if the issue persisted, they would require us to produce it again. With an intermitent issue, you can imagine how many times we took it in just to reproduce the issue. For us it would happen numerous times a week. We we're lucky to get it to happen on the day we took our vehicle in for the issue. We did reproduce the issue numerous times but Volvo could never figure it out. All they tried was force balancing all the wheels. They spoke to many of their engineers but never really did much. It got so bad that the car felt unsafe so we ended up getting rid of the vehicle. We lost $8k of our own money in doing so. One thing my wife and I commented on was, we never thought Volvo was this bad. We had always thought Volvo had a good name. But man, they we're so terrible. We did everything we could short of hiring an attorney. We called Orange County Volvo where we bought the vehicle to see what they would do. And all they did  was try to sell us a new XC90. I don't normally post reviews of any kind, good or bad. But this experience has just been so terrible and we lost so much money on this vehicle. I would want to know of problems like this before making a purchase. I've never been treated like this from any manufacturer. I have to say, this by far was the worst vehicle I have ever owned and the worst manufacturer by far. I would never purchase any sort of Volvo again.<//Text><username>Brett Cadiente< /username></record></dataset><record>

< review>
I had a 2007 S80 that i purchased brand new. The service department was always friendly but over the past couple of years they have had a lot of turn over. i faithfully took my car here for servicings. I never took my car anywhere else, because who best to work on a Volvo than the dealership. At times the repairs were ridiculous, like the time my inside driver door handle  melted from the heat and came off in my hand, or twice i had to repair a mechanism for the trunk. One of which was $700 to repair. But the biggest let down of all was their inability or unwillingness to help me maintain my transmission during the many times i took the car there for servicing. Not once a recommendation to even change the fluid. I figure if i am taking it to you as scheduled you are going to tell me what the car needs.  In the last 13 month period I spent almost $5000 on repairs and servicings, one of which was to help me figure out a problem that i was bringing to their attention, I described it every way I possibly could,  although the car was running fine, i knew something was wrong. $2000 later i have paid for 4 axles, but that turned out not to be the problem. However, when i picked up the car, it broke down on me 20 minutes later in the middle of the 5 freeway at 8:30 in the morning and they had to send someone to rescue me. A month later i bring it back for the same problem and they can't find anything wrong with it after keeping it 3 days. 6 months later I take it to another shop, The Auto Service on Grand in Santa Ana, and 4 hrs later i am told my transmission needs to be replaced. $4500 brand new and $1800 in labor. The guy didn't even try to talk me into having the repair done, but he also said my transmission fluid was black and he didn't think it had ever been serviced. How could this be when i had major servicings at 55,000 miles, 100,000 miles and 150,000 -- plus all the ones in between. I should have been able to get 300,000 miles out of my car instead after 10 years and 186,000 miles i had to give it up. I refused to put in a new transmission. ADVISEMENT - If you have a Volvo that is more than 5 years old, take it to John at The Auto Service. He knows a ton about Volvo, including all the old dogs who don't work on them anymore. This new breed is all about leasing and trading them in. They have absolutely no interest in helping you keep your Volvo long term. I wrote the General Manager a very detailed letter 6 weeks ago and have yet to hear a word back. Maybe my mistake was letting them know I had traded the car in. However, my biggest disappointment was their unwillingness or inability to be honest and  effective. I know replacing a transmission is a pain in the butt and no one wants to give a customer that news, but if i had been offered or recommended any transmission servicings during my many servicings, i probably would have been able to keep my car. The current mechanics are in my opinion completely inept, when it comes to working on something that requires  more than a routine servicing and is of age. Remember Volvo owners, if you have a Volvo that is more than 5 years old, there is help out there, see John at Auto Service on Grand. Excellent reviews. He didn't even charge me for the diagnostic, oh how I wish i had known about him years before.< /review>

<rating>5<//rating>< Review>
Latino's Meat Market is a hidden gem. This market has been the anchor of West Grand Avenue for many years. Businesses have come and gone but they remain. Tony and his staff always provide excellent customer service. The hot homemade-like food coming out of the kitchen is awesome. This includes the TJ-style street tacos, birria, menudo and tamales. I have had Latino's cater baptisms and birthdays. If you like grilling, the butcher shop is great too. The prices are very reasonable. I highly recommend you give Latino's Meat Market a try. You will not be disappointed!<//Review>

<Rating>5</Rating>< text>
This is really a fun place to go shop and to eat.. The grocery is pretty varied on what is on the shelves. Some stuff you're get a definitely miss it if you're looking for something like a major Supermarket.

However it does carry specialty stuff from food of Latin origin and also some Asian.   It's a fun experience to roam the shelves if you're a person who likes to cook .

What really shines here is the Meet Counter and the food  they prepare in their kitchen . Any place you want to look around the meat counter is absolutely gorgeous & it's perfectly cleaning. Their is knife work is beautiful. The guys behind the counter are very knowledgeable, very helpful, and courteous.

Courtesy in the atmosphere of a small friendly store that's loved by the neighborhood. Often on the way in you are greeted at the door and they make you extremely welcome.

In the store and they also have a kitchen and they prepared amazing Mexican food that include tacos, burritos, tamales,-soup mature assembly some of my favorites that are part of the menu.  The food is tasty, well-prepared and is price for a reasonably. I love this place.</text>

<UserId.>101322665937897630163<//UserId.>< Name>
Jazz Baruela< /Name>
<Date>1437921897608< /Date>< Rating>
4<//Rating>
<text>A friend of mine was brought me to this place after we had a mild-intense hike. Super hungry and craving Japanese food we came upon Sushi 29.

As you walk in the place you notice it's modern Japanese. It was very quiet and for me walking in shorts and a tank top I felt a little out of place. Our server was prompt and we all ordered; I'm going to base this review on my own experience.

When we told our server we'll be taking separate checks she told us we can split the check up to three ways which was perfect for us. I ordered a California Roll ($5) and a Unagi Don ($15).

The California roll was a piece of art and love. The way it was presented looked too goo to eat and when I did eat it I noticed right away this is not a generic California roll. This roll was made with real crab. Oh my goodness!!! Every piece was delectable, so excited for the unagi don. That came out soon after and more than I felt bad about eating it (because eel is being over-fished and there is actually a shortage, so it correlates with why it was expensive as it is) but it was flavorful.

The unagi sauce was soaked by the rice and you can see the layers of unagi, rice with the sauce, and the rice. My only complaints are I didn't have enough rice, but that's besides the point, I could have ordered more and the server didn't point out the lunch menu. If she did I wouldn't have spent $20;  reason I gave this place a 4 star. There are other options well under $10 on the lunch menu, totally would take advantage of that next time.

Solano Ave has a lot of eateries to try, I recommend Sushi 29  if you have a budget, looking for a nice sit-down restaurant, and want to try Japanese food in a more artistic dimension.<//text><Pics>None< /Pics>< Resp>
None< /Resp>

< text>
Boot barn has a large selection of western and outdoor apparel. They have everything from belts, boots and buckles to jeans, jackets, and coveralls. "Low level" to high level brands carried and not much of difference in price. If shopping specifically for boots, know what you need and are looking for or you will get lost in their vast selection. They have help roaming to assist but ultimately only you will know which boots are the ones meant for you. They also have a 2nd floor level with what looks like the ladies apparel. Customer service was okay and parking was cramped & scarce. Early mornings and late evens before closing are the best times to shop. I will still come back because of their selection despite pricing being cheaper online at places like Amazon. Fitting is key.< /text>
